  <script type="text/javascript">
    (function() {
        var contextPath = '/jira';
        var eventBuffer = [];

        function printDeprecatedMsg() {
            if (console && console.warn) {
                console.warn('DEPRECATED JS - contextPath global variable has been deprecated since 7.4.0. Use `wrm/context-path` module instead.');
            }
        }

        function sendEvent(analytics, postfix) {
            analytics.send({
                name: 'js.globals.contextPath.' + postfix
            });
        }

        function sendDeprecatedEvent(postfix) {
            try {
                var analytics = require('jira/analytics');
                if (eventBuffer.length) {
                    eventBuffer.forEach(function(value) {
                        sendEvent(analytics, value);
                    });
                    eventBuffer = [];
                }

                if (postfix) {
                    sendEvent(analytics, postfix);
                }
            } catch(ex) {
                eventBuffer.push(postfix);
                setTimeout(sendDeprecatedEvent, 1000);
            }
        }

        Object.defineProperty(window, 'contextPath', {
            get: function() {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('get');
                return contextPath;
            },
            set: function(value) {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('set');
                contextPath = value;
            }
        });
    })();

</script>

               <div id="descriptionmodule_heading" class="mod-header">
                <ul class="ops"></ul>
                <h2 class="toggle-title">Description</h2>
               </div>
               <div class="mod-content">
                <div id="description-val" class="field-ignore-highlight"> 
                 <div class="user-content-block"> 
                  <p>Here's a patch that implements simple support of Lucene's MoreLikeThis class.</p> 
                  <p>The MoreLikeThisHelper code is heavily based on (hmm..."lifted from" might be more appropriate <img class="emoticon" src="/jira/images/icons/emoticons/wink.png" height="16" width="16" align="absmiddle" alt="" border="0"> Erik Hatcher's example mentioned in <a href="http://www.mail-archive.com/solr-user@lucene.apache.org/msg00878.html" class="external-link" rel="nofollow">http://www.mail-archive.com/solr-user@lucene.apache.org/msg00878.html</a></p> 
                  <p>To use it, add at least the following parameters to a standard or dismax query:</p> 
                  <p> mlt=true<br> mlt.fl=list,of,fields,which,define,similarity</p> 
                  <p>See the MoreLikeThisHelper source code for more parameters.</p> 
                  <p>Here are two URLs that work with the example config, after loading all documents found in exampledocs in the index (just to show that it seems to work - of course you need a larger corpus to make it interesting):</p> 
                  <p><a href="http://localhost:8983/solr/select/?stylesheet=&amp;q=apache&amp;qt=standard&amp;mlt=true&amp;mlt.fl=manu,cat&amp;mlt.mindf=1&amp;mlt.mindf=1&amp;fl=id,score" class="external-link" rel="nofollow">http://localhost:8983/solr/select/?stylesheet=&amp;q=apache&amp;qt=standard&amp;mlt=true&amp;mlt.fl=manu,cat&amp;mlt.mindf=1&amp;mlt.mindf=1&amp;fl=id,score</a></p> 
                  <p><a href="http://localhost:8983/solr/select/?stylesheet=&amp;q=apache&amp;qt=dismax&amp;mlt=true&amp;mlt.fl=manu,cat&amp;mlt.mindf=1&amp;mlt.mindf=1&amp;fl=id,score" class="external-link" rel="nofollow">http://localhost:8983/solr/select/?stylesheet=&amp;q=apache&amp;qt=dismax&amp;mlt=true&amp;mlt.fl=manu,cat&amp;mlt.mindf=1&amp;mlt.mindf=1&amp;fl=id,score</a></p> 
                  <p>Results are added to the output like this:<br> &lt;response&gt;<br> ...<br> &lt;lst name="moreLikeThis"&gt;<br> &lt;result name="UTF8TEST" numFound="1" start="0" maxScore="1.5293242"&gt;<br> &lt;doc&gt;<br> &lt;float name="score"&gt;1.5293242&lt;/float&gt;<br> &lt;str name="id"&gt;SOLR1000&lt;/str&gt;<br> &lt;/doc&gt;<br> &lt;/result&gt;<br> &lt;result name="SOLR1000" numFound="1" start="0" maxScore="1.5293242"&gt;<br> &lt;doc&gt;<br> &lt;float name="score"&gt;1.5293242&lt;/float&gt;<br> &lt;str name="id"&gt;UTF8TEST&lt;/str&gt;<br> &lt;/doc&gt;<br> &lt;/result&gt;<br> &lt;/lst&gt;</p> 
                  <p>I haven't tested this extensively yet, will do in the next few days. But comments are welcome of course.</p> 
                 </div> 
                </div> 
               </div>
              </div>

If the MLT results are added as \\\"tier 2\\\" data to StandardRequestHandler response, then all of the other \\\"tier 2\\\" data blocks (highlighting, faceting, debugQuery score explanation, etc..) still refer to the main result from the original query ... this may be what you want in use case #2, but doesn\'t really make sense for use case #1, where the \\\"tier 1\\\" main result only contains the single document you asked for by id ... the score explanation and facet count numbers aren\'t very interesting in that case.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003efor case #1, what you really want is for the MLT data to be treated as the primary (\\\"tier 1\\\") result set, and all of hte \\\"tier 2\\\" data is about those results ... highlighting is done on the MLT docs, facet counts are for the MLT docs, debugQuery score explanation tells you \u003cb\u003ewhy\u003c\\/b\u003e the MLT docs are like your original docs, etc..\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eCase #1 and case #2 are both useful, to address Brian\'s 02\\/May\\/07 comment..\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e &gt; I\'ve personally never understood the \\\"more documents \u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n &gt; that don\'t match this query but are like the documents \u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n &gt; in this query\\\" ... And would the original query results get \u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n &gt; returned? What\'s the ordering? \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003ein your example, yes ... the users main search on \\\"apache\\\" would return 10 results sorted by whatever sort they specified.  for each of docs right there on the main result page, you still need to execute the MLT logic as part of hte initial request to know if there there are \u003cb\u003eany\u003c\\/b\u003e similar docs (so you can surface the link\\/button for displaying them to the user.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI would even argue there is actually a third use case ... set.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003ecase#2 would still easily be handled by having some new \\\"tier 2\\\" MLT data added to the StandardRequestHandler.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n subsequent list of similar \\\"mlt\\\" documents that have things in common with all of the docs in the current page of results displayed elsewhere on the page. \\n&#8211; \\n\\n ...where case #2 is about having separate MLT lists for each of hte matching reuslts, this case is about having a single \\\"if you are interested in  all  of these items, you might also be interested in these other items\\\" list. \\n\\n case#1 and case#3 can both easily be satisfied with a single \\\"MoreLikeThisHandler\\\" which takes as it\'s input a generic query (ie: \\\"q=id:12345\\\" for case#1, and
